After I have finished with you, my Son, this book which is the most recent of my works in medicine, completed with the addition of the present treatise, and following the exposition of its parts and the statements of its author, I have deemed it fitting to present to you this work which is a part of the art of surgery, namely surgery with the hand.
Since surgery with the hand is a matter of great importance in our times and in our age, and since it is a subject which has been neglected for a long time: except for a few scattered descriptions in the ancient books, which have been altered by the hand itself: there has arisen a great error and hesitation, until the intentions of the art have been closed and its science prolonged. It seemed good to me to restore life to this art with the help of the ordination of this treatise according to its position, declaration and abbreviation: and to bring together the forms of the instruments of cautery and other implements of the art, with the addition of their declaration and the improvement of their preparation which is necessary.
The reason why one does not easily find a good surgeon of his hand in our time is that the art of medicine is long, and the author must exercise himself beforehand in the science of anatomy as Galen has narrated, until he knows the movements of the limbs, their forms, and their connection, and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, lacerations, and the number of each, and their exit, and the pulse of the veins, and quietness, and the locations of their exits
And for this reason Hippocrates said, "A name is nothing in itself, but in its work it is much.
We have indeed mentioned this in the beginning of this book.
For he who is ignorant of the science of anatomy will fall into error, and will endanger human life. As for me, I have seen many who have puffed up with pride about this science without any knowledge or experience
Why did the doctor order the securing of the swelling in the woman's neck with a scrofula, since it involved the incisions of some arteries in the neck? Because of this, blood flowed from the woman until she died between her hands.
And the other physician thought that he should remove a stone which was in the urine, which was causing her pain, and the stone was large. Therefore he came to him and extracted it with the bladder stone Because the man died on the third day.
And indeed I was called to extract it: and I saw from the size of the stone and the condition of the patient that he would die
And another physician saw that a certain Duke of our land had taken a medicine: and it happened to the black eunuch who was with him that he fractured his leg near the ankle: and the physician, with his ignorance, bound the fracture with nails and pins, and did not allow the wound to drain.
And he died according to his desires. Then he dismissed him after a few days and commanded him not to move the ligament: and he stood thus until the swelling of his leg was gone, and his foot and leg together, and he came to his end
I was called to him again: and I set about resolving the ligament: and there was peace, and he was freed from his pains
But indeed the corruption was confirmed in the limb: and I could not restrain it.
Therefore the corruption ceased to advance in the limb until it died.
And another physician saw that he perforated a cancerous swelling: and it ulcerated after a few days, until the malignancy of the disease increased with the master himself
When the cancer is pure and arises from melancholic humour, it must not be held together with iron throughout, except in the member which can tolerate it, in order that the whole of it may be excised.
And for this reason, my son, you must know that an operation is divided into two parts: namely, the operation which is associated with health, and the operation which carries the risk in various conditions.
I am excited about all the places in this book where the operation is mentioned which carries terror and fear.
Therefore you must be careful about this, and fear it: so that they do not find pride in speaking falsely, and be dishonest
Receive therefore measure with humility and protection, and the sick with ease and firmness, and use the better way that brings glory to God for the healing and praiseworthy succession: and send away the terrifying diseases that are difficult to cure: and take away the spirits of those who make you fear, so that there should appear no hesitation in your faith and comfort for you
For in this way remains the measure of your glory, and the sublimation in this world, and afterwards to the quantity of your souls
For Galen has said in some of his admonitions. You do not heal a bad disease: do not call a bad doctor by name
I have however divided this treatise into three chapters.
First chapter.
Of cautery with fire, and cautery with acute medicine, a chapter, and arranged from the head to the feet, and forms of instruments, and materials for cautery: and everything that is necessary for the operation.
Second Chapter.
On section and perforation, phlebotomy and packing, wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and things of that sort: and the whole chapter, arranged in the form of instruments.
Third Chapter.
On restoration, and dislocation, and the treatment of twisting, and things of that sort: the whole chapter, arranged from the head to the feet, and the form of instruments.
But before anything else that we remember of an operation, it is necessary to say what is the quality of the dressings and instruments: and in what complexion it should be shown
I say therefore, that the discourse concerning the quality of the cautery dressing and instrument is a profound, subtle, scientific, and occult discourse.
And it has been spoken by many learned men in this matter, and they have disagreed among themselves: and indeed little is sufficient from their discourses, fearing the prolongation of the discourse.
I say therefore, that the cautery is universal in all complexion, which is with matter and without matter: except for two complexions, which are the hot complexion without matter, and the dry complexion without matter
In the hot and dry complexion with matter they disagree among themselves. Some indeed say that the cautery is useful in these. Others have also said that Cauterium is not suitable for an ailment caused by heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat: and it is inappropriate to cure a heat and dry ailment with heat and dryness.
Others have also said that Cauterium causes injury in all heat and dry ailments which occur in the bodies of men: for when you compare the body of a man with fire, and moisten it, you find the body of a man to be cold
I too have heard from experience that this is the case.
It is true that one must not proceed without first having learned, practiced in the last exercise of the Cauterium chapter, recognized the diversity of human complexions, and become acquainted with the causes and effects of ailments, and their times
The rest, however, of complexions is not dangerous: especially in cold and wet ailments. I myself have seen all physicians agree about this: and they do not refrain from using Cauterium in these ailments.
And behold, the sons have said: The secret of treatment by Cauterium with fire is better than the secret of treatment with burning medicine: for fire is simple, whose action does not remain except on the member which is cauterized: and it does not harm any other connected member except for a slight burn.
Burning medicine, however, has an action that extends beyond the member which is being cauterized: and perhaps causes difficulty in the healing of the ailment in the member itself, and perhaps brings about death.
Fire, however, on account of its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not do this, except in excess.
I am now convinced by experience, through the length of my service and study with art, and the position over truth of things: and because of this, I am excused from the length of the oration.
And if this is not sufficient, since it is not permitted for this book of mine, I will declare a secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies expelled by it, which expels diseases with philosophical demonstration, agreeable to the thoughts of the wise.
And know ye, my sons, that they themselves dissent in the time when it becomes necessary to make the cautery, and they advise me to make a better time of your work.
I say that the cautery is suitable for all times: for indeed the document grows dull through the passage of time, which is attracted by the cautery.</start_of_turn> And above all, if the cautery is for necessary and severe pains, which are urgent, which do not tolerate delay: for indeed they fear from the fire that arises from the evil which increases more than the slight dullness which the document suffers through the passage of time.</start_of_turn>
And let it not be thought by anyone, my sons, or any doctor, that because of this I do not esteem the learned and skilled physicians, for indeed the sickness which is cured by the cautery is not always the same: and they put this in consequence, and it is not so as they think: for the cautery is not, except in the place of medicine, which alters the complexion and dries up humours which are the causes of the disease.</start_of_turn
But indeed the cautery surpasses medicine by the swiftness of its action, the excellence of its operation, and the extent of its mastery: and it is possible that the disease will vanish at some later time according to the complexion of the patient, the location of the disease, and the excellence of the treatment: and that which is prepared in his body from the collection of superfluous humours in him: and that which proceeds from the disease itself in its acquisition from foods and like things, except in the case of those diseases in which the cautery is administered.</start_of_turn
Acute pain in a limb with few superficial wounds, and moisture, like a tooth cautery due to pain, is possible, lest it return in that place with pain. But this is done in few cases.</start_of_turn>
Indeed, the word often returns, for the cautery is the most recent of medicine. It is the right word: not for what they wish for it, for they believe that there is no cure that can be compared with medicine, neither with anything after the cautery.</start_of_turn>
The thing, however, is contrary to that. For the intention of the cautery being the most recent of medicine is not, except when we employ other modes of treatment in some ailment, and these do not confer that healing: we then apply the cautery at the end of everything, and that does confer. From that time forward, because the cautery is the most recent of medicine, not according to the intention which the vulgar people and many learned physicians understand.</start_of_turn>
The ancients said that the cautery with gold is better than with iron: and they did not say that except because of the equality of the gold and the fineness of its substance. And they said that it does not form pus at the place of the cautery.</start_of_turn> But this is not absolutely true. For I have seen that it does not cause this in some bodies without other things.</start_of_turn>
And the cautery with the instrument itself is good, and better than with iron, as they said.</start_of_turn But when you apply the cautery with fire from gold, you must not declare that it has been kindled according to the quantity you wish, because of the redness of the gold: and when it approaches the cold and you add to it the fire from below, it liquefies in the fire, and turns into plates.</start_of_turn
Why does the artificer depart from this work in pursuit of his business? And because of this, Cauterium is made with iron among us more rapid and proximate to the operation, from rectitude to the work.
I also command this chapter on Cauterium to be read, following the chapters: and I command these things from the head to the feet: so that they may satisfy anyone who seeks anything from this.
Chapter 2: On the cauterization of the head in the coronal suture
Here is cauterization is made to the lord of humidity and cold over the brain: which are two causes of sweat, and the multitude of flow of humors from the head to the parts of the eyes and ears, and the multitude of sleep, and toothache, and throat pain: and in general all ailments which arise from cold, such as paralysis, and sweat, and seizures, and apoplexy, and things similar to these from ailments.
The method of cauterization is as follows: when the patient is most feverish: when he is evacuated at first with a physician who gives a medicinal salve to the head for three nights, or four, according to the nature of the patient, his age, and his habits.
Then command him to make a mark on his head with a needle. Then make him sit between your hands square, so that you can put your hands on his chest
Then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes Wherever your middle finger reaches, that is the place to make the burn with the cautery
Then ignite Cauterium with olive oil: thus is its form
Then place it upon the marked place with an incision, and let it descend gradually, so that your hand may withdraw it slowly. Then draw out your hand quickly and look at the place
If you see any amount of bone or herb remaining, then draw out your hand. And if not, repeat drawing out your hand with the instrument, or with another one if it is cold: until you see the bones, as I have said to you.
Then take some salt and dissolve it in water, and drink from it, and put it upon the place: and leave it for three days.
Then put upon it butter soaked in oil, and leave the bandage above the place until the eschar is consumed by fire. Then care for it with unguents of four herbs, until it is healed
I have said that the more the wound remains open, the more pus it emits: which is better and more advantageous
And some people say that the skin should be cauterized until the bone is reached: and hold the Cauterium until something of the thickness of an os is burnt.
Then withdraw after that which has been burned from the bone, and then care for it
And some say that it is necessary that the Cauterium should remain until the very end, until it has left an imprint in the bone like a mark of the alphabet, so that the bone is fractured: or that a woman should put an instrument infused with a small letter into the wound: and they say that it should be withdrawn when the vapor of the head escapes from this place for a long time
Then he cares until consolidated.
Neither of two kinds of cautery is used in all men, except in some in whom it is feared according to their temperaments.
And dismiss it; it is better with me for the health of the patient
The head weakens from the continuity of its natural solution: as we have witnessed in the rest of the limbs: and especially when the head of the patient is weak by nature: for the first kind of cautery is more safe and better with me, and this is what is useful: to work with it for the health of the patient.
Head Chapter III.
When in the whole head there occurs a chronic pain that lasts in the patient, and it is accompanied by fever, and swelling, and blisters, and oils, and other things are used for it And especially if it has already been cauterized once with the cautery which we mentioned, and nothing more is added to it: then consider it For if the head of the patient is strong in creation by nature, and is not weak, and if there is inflammation: then cauterize with another cautery under that little bit Then cauterize it over all the hairs of the head with the cautery, so that it does not penetrate the skin, and uncover only the quantity of bone that we have mentioned And cauterize it once with the cautery in the nape of the neck of the head, in the place which is called the uas: and this is the place where the marrow is placed: and raise the mat of hair in this, and do not uncover the bone The sick man finds it on account of that pain which he suffers, and diverse from the rest of the pains of the head.
And I say that this Cauterium is in its place: and it is necessary that it be Cauterium, with which the horns of the head and its occiput are cauterized, and the middle part of the head is cauterized more finely
Chapter III
When it happens in the part of the head that there is pain and heat, or that the pain extends to the eye, and it is evacuated with medicines that soothe the head, and the rest of the treatment is administered as I have said in the discussion of diseases, and it does not suffice for it: then cauterization is done in two ways: either with acute burning medicine or with an iron.</start_of_turn>
But as for cauterization with acute burning medicine, that is, that you take a tooth of the other side and burn the surface of the cauterization, and cut off its extremities from both sides.</start_of_turn Then cut off the place of pain in time with a wide vein cut, until there is in that place under the skin, where the tooth is caught.</start_of_turn
Introduce it into that place under the skin, until it is hidden: then bind up above it with a bandage of constriction, and leave it for fifteen hours, then take it out, and wash away the pus. Afterwards put over it a soaked cushion in butter, until the place has healed. Then care for it with ointment until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
And if anyone wishes to do this with some of the physicians who burn [medicines], as I wrote in the twelfth tractate, on Physicians who endure.
Burning with iron is indeed done in this way.</start_of_turn> The iron is ignited in this fashion.</start_of_turn>
And it is called Clavius: because its shape is like the head of a key, in which there is some curvature, and in the middle of it there is a small protrusion.</start_of_turn
Then place it over the place and hold your hand: and gradually withdraw the iron with speed: and let the quantity which endures from the thickness of the skin be as much as half of it.</start_of_turn And lift your hand, so that the artery beneath does not burn, and blood flow does not occur.</start_of_turn
Then soak the wound in salt water, and place over the place, and leave it for three days: then place the wound with butter: afterwards care with ointment until it has healed.</start_of_turn>
And if necessary, burn this hemibranium with the second extremity of the knife of Cautery.</start_of_turn Burn from the incision of the artery in this half-brain, not in the old way.</start_of_turn
In the old way of cautery in the half-brain.</start_of_turn
When you have cured the half-brain, when that which we said concerning the treatment of ailments has been done, and when we have said concerning the precautions for diseases, and it does not suffice: and if you see from the disease that it does not suffice with the first cautery with medicine, or with the cautery with fire, then you must burn the Cautery knife until the sign of relief appears on the place of pain with a line whose length is half of a digit, or like this: and put your hand away quickly once, and tighten it until you have cut the artery, and keep it until the bone.</start_of_turn
It is necessary to restrain you, so that you do not cause the continuation of the jaw, which moves during mastication, lest it become swollen or the nerve which moves it be damaged, from which results spasm.
Take also great care of the guarding of the artery which has been cut off, and of the flow of blood from it.</start_of_turn> In the cutting of it there is fear, especially for the one who is ignorant of this and is careless and unlearned: he lets the operation go from his hands at the first.</start_of_turn>

On the manner of cauterizing in the pain of the ears.</start_of_turn
When it happens in the ear a pain from the cold, and it is cured with solutions, and the rest of the cure as we have said in the treatise, and the pain is not removed, then ignite Cauterium: and that is called Punctum, which has this shape.</start_of_turn

And then care for the place until it heals.</start_of_turn>

Chapter VII.</start_of_turn>
The Torment which is cured by Cauterization is not except from the kinds which happen from phlegmas, as we said in the discourse of the causes of diseases.</start_of_turn
And you must Cauterize the kind which happens from exication and spasm of the nerve.</start_of_turn
When you have cured this kind of torment with urine, and purging-pills, and hiccups, and the cure does not suffice, then it is necessary to Cauterize the patient three times with the Cautery: once at the root of the ear, and the second a little lower from the ear, and the third at the junction of the two lips.</start_of_turn
And put the Cautery on the side opposite the infirm part.</start_of_turn For the softening does not take place except in the part which appears healthy.</start_of_turn
And the form of the Cauterization is that you Cauterize with the Cautery itself at the tip of the upper ear under the ear-wax of the little horn: and the other at the ear-root. The length of each is as long as the thumb.</start_of_turn And put your hand away with the Cautery, until the quantity of the middle part of the thickness of the skin is consumed.</start_of_turn
This is the form of the Cauter, and it is of the kind which has a blade whose form precedes it: it is not subtler than water in this respect. And the blade must be of such a size as to suffice for the thickness of the tissue.
Then take care of the place where the operation has been made: until it is healed.
As for cauterization in ancient Apoplexia.
When the ancient Apoplexia has become established, and when your treatment has failed, and the patient has no fever, then cauterize four times over every horn of the head, and cauterize in the middle of the head, as we have said, and cauterize in the back of the head, as it has been shown: and the manner of cauterization must be as we have said.</start_of_turn>
The cauterization is also done with the Cauter over the bone of the stomach: and this is the last method.</start_of_turn

Head X.
It is necessary to proceed in the mollification of the head with lye, and as we have said
Then remove the head of the patient: afterwards cauterize the middle of the head, and the horns of the head, and the back of the head, and three on the bones of the neck.
If however you find in the softening of the body by these many, and the patient is tolerant, and the swelling is great: then make four Cauteriums over the bones of the back, and the last one with a Cauterium, until it burns from the greater part of its surface, and lift up your hand Then care for it until it is healed: and keep the Cauterium oiled.
In case of Epilepsy
The epileptic head is not cauterized, except for the one whose epilepsy proceeds from phlegm.
It is necessary therefore that the physician should temper the violent action of the brain in the first place with opium, and afterwards with the other treatments which we mentioned in the preceding chapter: for when the patient is great or suffers from the action of many medicines.
If, however, the patient is young and cannot tolerate the medicines, there is administered a gargling-drink, and biting medicines which temper the action of the brain, for many days before with the restoration of the appetite of food
Then the head is treated with powder, and afterwards the cautery is applied once in the middle of the head, as has been said previously in its kind: and the cautery is applied once in the back of the head, and over every horn of the head there is applied the cautery If the patient should be strong and tolerant, then the cautery is applied with oil, as has been said previously.
If the patient is young, then the cautery is applied softly, as has been said above.
Method of cauterizing in melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupt humours, and thick phlegm, then the cautery is applied as has been said in the case of palsy
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of wine which leads to melancholy, and the body of the patient is soft and wet, then give him something which will temper the action of the brain, as has been mentioned in the preceding chapter: then treat the head of the patient, and afterwards make a circle from the centre of the head made of linen.
Then place it in the middle of the head: and the sitting patient is held fast from every side.
Then present the unguents. And it is better from old butter or oil And warm it over gentle fire, as much as the finger tolerates when it is introduced into it Then evacuate it in the middle of his head in a circle, and hold it until it is cold
Do this to the patient every week once, with the rest of his treatment being good, until he is healed
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small holes in it, except that you hold the hand with the cautery: for it will smell.
For this kind of cautery hydrates the brain with its quality
Then place over it a cushion soaked in butter, or fat from a chicken
So cauterize in descending water to the eye
Chapter XIII
When the beginning of water in the eye is declared by the signs which I mentioned in the explanation, then begin and pour out the patient, along with what will temper his head
And keep him away from all humilities, and make him sit in a bath, for a few days
Then order him to raise his head, and cauterize it in the middle of his head. If you see that anything from it has escaped, then immediately cut it off with whatever medicine is available: and I shall come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and the cutting off of them, and the care of the blood flow.
And when it is cauterized on the bone, under two bones, two last cauterizations are produced

Chapter XVII.</start_of_turn
There are two kinds of cautery: either with fire or with burning medicine.</start_of_turn
But in the cautery with fire, it is necessary to warn the patient beforehand so that he may expel his hairs, if there are any which are moving, until they are prolonged and equal.</start_of_turn If, however, the patient has them at the root of their eye: then bind his eyes with wool, so that they do not move, until they have healed.</start_of_turn
When they have healed and are equal, then put the head of the patient in your lap: then sign over the Palpebra of his eye with ink, in the form of the leaf of the Myrtle: and let the beginning of the sign be near the eyelashes.</start_of_turn
Then place the soaked cushion in albumin or: on the mucus of the eyelashes above the eye.
Then apply the cautery, which is of this shape.
Then burn over the figure which you indicated gradually in many places, until the surface of the skin is burnt, which is like the figure of a myrtle leaf, throughout its appearance
And the sign of the completion of your work is: if you touch the Palpebra of the eye with your finger and pull out the hair at the point of the eye.
Withdraw your hand then: and discharge him in three days.
Then place upon it a cushion with butter, until the eschar is eradicated Then care for it with unguent until it is healed.
If some hair should remain after an hour, and the Palpebra be softened: then repeat the cautery over the place as you did at first.
If they are in the lower parts: then burn the area until the hair is raised to its natural place: and make it even so that the hair does not pierce the eye
It is necessary for the sickly person to remove the hair, until they become prolonged and even Make from parchment a shape like a myrtle leaf
Then take from soap that has been boiled, and from burnt lime without soaking from one pound about an ounce and a quarter: then mix these together with a good hand, and make it so that it does not freeze Then take from the end of the vein above the mark which you made like the form of a myrtle leaf, and place it upon the eyeball of one, or two. And place under the eye the soaked cotton in albumin: and the head of the patient be in your hand.
And place your finger on the mark over the medicine, and press it slightly. And you will move it whenever the patient feels the biting of the medicine: because its biting is like fire.
While therefore you have persisted in this, when you find the biting, then remove the medicine, and move it with your finger. When the biting has ceased, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And consider then, if the eyeball is relaxed after the expansion, like that which is raised at the contraction with fire, or with incision, it is good: and if not, then repeat over the medicine on the place where the medicine does not touch, without damaging it, until the operation be accomplished, and the eye be contracted
Then place upon it a cotton ball with butter, until the skin of the wound be scraped away Then care for it with ointment of diaphonius, or something else, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you in the operation, that you take care of the last care, that nothing of the medicine should fall into the eye
Because if the eyeball becomes soft after days, and there is something gritty in the eye from the hair, then repeat the medicine on the place where the eyeball is softened by itself, like you did at first. Then care for it until it is healed
This is the form of the Myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men differ in size and shape Therefore, you must take this into consideration: and it is not concealed by the uprightness of the art, which is the study of this craft
As for the cauterization of the fistula of the tear duct
When you have treated the fistula, when you have done what we said in the instructions for the aetiologies, and the cure does not result: then you must cauterize it according to this method.
Command the patient to put his head in your lap, and hold his head between your hands like this, so that it does not move or shake with his head
Then put the sponge soaked in urine or in the mucus of the hair on his eye: then apply the Cauterium, which is of this shape
Let it be concave, like the shape of a feather from its extremity to the other, as Cauterium is made: and if you wish it to penetrate until the other extremity, or if you wish it to be above, do so as you please
It is better to make it concave for your work
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and extract from it the pus, and dry it up: and if it is not open, then open it up, and extract the pus from it.
Then put on it again the Cauterium, which is made burning slightly.
Hold your hand nearby the Cauterium from the eye to the part of the nose, so that your hand does not slip or trouble the patient: and place the Cauterium on the fat of the eye, and consume it.
If indeed you proceed with the Cauterization from the beginning until the bone, it will be well. Or if not: then repeat the Cauterization once or twice if it does not suffice: and discharge it in three days.
Then apply a compress with butter, and care for it with an unguent poultice until it heals.
If after forty days it does not heal: then apply an acute corrosive medicine above it until the bone is exposed: and then proceed according to what is written in its chapter
And there is another method of Cauterization of fistulas, which some of the first men mentioned. Aim at the location of the fistula and find it: then place under the fistula a small cushion, that is, a cannula of a small size, whose shape is this And pour into it the quantity of drachmas of liquid lead, and keep your hand firmly clasped with the cannula, and do not move the patient at all, so that it does not run, or that the liquid lead should not reach his eye
And it is necessary to place over the eye of the patient a compress soaked in fat or in water.
Lead will consume the place of the fistula, and will heal it with a miraculous healing
And if the fistula is healed, with what we have said concerning Cauterization and treatment, it is good Or if not, it is necessary to administer a nose-opening passage, and reduce the fistula to the curvature of the nose, according to what is proper in its own place
On the manner of cauterizing of lip-fissures.
Many accidents occur in the lip concerning a fissure, which are called Pili, and especially in the lips of children.
When you are treating these fissures, as we mentioned in the discourse about ailments, and the cure does not suffice, then you must cauterize slightly with a small knife, according to this shape
And let the cavity be equal to the thickness of the knife
Then put the fire quickly on these fissures until the cauterium reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then care for it with oil until it heals.
Thus cauterize in the fistula of the lip.
When swelling occurs in the root of the tooth, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then pus forms, and it bursts: afterwards it becomes hardened, and pus runs out, and a fistula forms: then you must treat the fistula itself, and not the swelling, then it is necessary to cauterize according to the quantity which is in the fistula Then introduce the fire into the cavity of the fistula and hold your hand, until the fire reaches the depth of it, and the end of it: do this once or twice.
Then care for it afterwards as we mentioned about the cure until it heals
If it bursts spontaneously, and heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to remove the corrupted bone according to what comes to light in the head
Thus cauterize in the gums and soften the teeth.
When the gums are swollen from moisture, and the teeth are loosened, and care is taken with the physicians, and it does not help: then put the patient's head in your lap.
Then ignite the cautery, whose form will appear afterwards, so that you can place the cautery upon the tooth: and introduce the flame into it quickly: and keep your hand steady, until the patient feels the heat of the fire to have reached the root of the tooth
And lift your hand: then repeat the cautery a few more times, as you please.
Then let the patient rinse his mouth with salt-water, and let him rinse for one hour: and then he shall spit it out.
The tooth will now be firm, and the gums will be softened and dried, and the moisture will be expelled.
Thus the cautery is to be used in toothache.
When the toothache is caused by cold, or if the tooth itself is cold or wet, and the treatment does not help with the physicians: then the cautery must be used in two ways: either with butter or with fire.
The cautery with butter is done by taking butter of the kind which is scraped off the calf, and mixing it with the yolk of an egg, and applying it to the tooth with a spatula Then take a sponge, and put it over the end of the tooth. Then plunge it into the boiling butter: and put it upon the painful tooth quickly, and hold it there until it cools: then repeat it a few more times, until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth
If desired, immerse the lancet in butter, or coat the heel in cold butter, and place it over the aching tooth: and place over it a burning iron until the fire has penetrated to the depth of the cavity.
The cauterization of it with fire is useful, so as to reach the air cavity, or the iron cavity And let there be in its body some breadth, so that the intensity of the fire does not reach the sound bone.
Then the cautery, which will take the form of this: place it over the tooth: and hold your hand until the cautery is cold.
Do this quickly, for pain will depart, or in the same day, or another day.
And it is necessary to impress the impression of the cautery, so that it may fill the sick bone with butter, and keep it for an hour: then spit it out
This is the form of the cautery
The cauterize with whatever extremity you will, as is possible: and this is the form of the cannula.
In this manner the cauterizing of the molars.
When the molars are affected by phlegmas, and by cold humilities, and do not obey digestion by medicines, and you wish to accelerate their digestion: then cauterize the cavity which has this shape.
Having two open extremities, so as to escape the smoke of the cautery from the other extremity: place the burning iron over the tooth once, and a second time, if you do not digest it, until it has penetrated to the depth of the cavity
If the fistula is small: then apply the Cauterium according to the quantity of the fistula.
Then discharge it for three days, and place above it a soaked cushion in butter, until it has recovered what the fire consumed
Then care for it with ointment of teeth, until it heals in the form of a tube.
In the swelling of the belly, and constriction of the breath.
When the belly becomes moist over the passage of the wind, and especially when it is with the coldness of the complexion: then it is necessary to evacuate the patient at once with the physicians who are accustomed to such things.
Then cauterize it in the night at the root of the gullet in a depressed place: and burn, do not bring near the Cauterium to the gullet, nor on the skin, except for something of that sort
Then cauterize it with another Cauterium at the juncture of the neck at the end of its last rib: and let the Cauterium be closed according to the mode which preceded it
Then care for it with that which preceded it, until it heals
In the ailments of the lungs, and of the breast.
When there is cough and pulmonary disease from cold humors, and the patient has neither fever nor phthisis, nor old cough: then cauterize it with two Cauteriums above the epiglottis in depressed places, in lenium, in the groove. And another Cauterium in the middle of the chest between the two nipples: and let the Cauterium be in the form of a tube as it preceded.
If one wishes to perform a cauterization by puncturing with the cautery, which is called Punctum, whose form precedes in the puncture of the ear: there should be punctures from thirty punctures up to almost as many.
Then take care of it with that which precedes, until it is healed
And if there is a cautery having three branches: according to this shape Therefore the cautery will be alleviated with that which is done with the three Cauteries when you make it with that liquid one time

Method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and much moisture are brought into the Stomach, until you have extracted it from its complex, and multiplied the catarrh upon it, and applied the methods of treatment diligently, and do not fear: then it is necessary for the sick man to lie upon his back, to extend his limbs, and to stretch out his hands Then cauterize with three cauteries, a cautery under the pectoralis angle measuring the quantity of one finger with a hook cautery, and two lower ones from two sides of one cautery, until the figure of the cauteries becomes triangular And lengthen between each other so that they do not join, when they produce pus.
And the depth of the cautery is the quantity of two-thirds of the thickness of the skin
And let the figure of the cauteries be in this shape without addition: and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this shape: and let the cautery be as this one which makes this cautery to be one according to the shape of the circle according to this shape

On the method of cauterizing the liver after-effects.
When this happens, and you are aware of it, if the after-effect is in the liver flesh or its covering: if it is in the liver flesh, there is mild pain and slight swelling without sharpness: and if it is in the liver covering, with sharp pain that extends upwards: know that the physician has become weary of its treatment.
Therefore it is necessary for the physician to rest the patient above the navel Then the figure of the after-effect is placed with the cautery: then the cautery is applied which is readily absorbed by the rays. This is its form And cauterize with one cautery until the whole skin is burnt, and it reaches the fat, until the whole wound is healed: then care for the after-effects until healing is complete
And do not let any other kind of cautery be used except that which is learned in the art of medicine: and by the hand of those who have experience in these matters: for otherwise you will hear of many such operations.
In this case, I would rather leave it alone.
On the method of cauterizing in the pleura.
The ancients say that cautery with the roots of aristolochia should be applied to the cold pleura according to this method. And it is like taking from the dry roots of aristolochia a long root, which comes from it, and be as thick as the breadth of a finger Then immerse the limb in oil: and raise it in fire. Then cauterize with one instrument at the point where the furcula joins the neck, and with two small cautery instruments under guidance slightly depressed to the part which is under the beard.
And also two cautery instruments at the point which is between the fifth and sixth ribs depressed downwards: and a cautery instrument at the middle of the chest, and one above the stomach And three cautery instruments from behind: one at the point which is between two ribs, and two at the two sides of the chest, the lower cautery being at the point which is between two ribs.
And do not press the hand with the cautery, but rather let the smell of the skin suffice.
And some ancient writers say that there are certain men who use a cautery like a rod of iron: they burn and throw it into the place between the ribs, until it is consumed by them to the very end, and comes out whole: as we said in the case of the Epiglottis.
But in this perforation with the cautery there is fear lest the patient should immediately die or that a fistula should occur in the place, which has no healing.
In this way cauterize the Spleen Head as follows:
When you are treating the pain of the spleen, when that treatment which we mentioned in the enumeration of diseases has not produced a cure, then you must cauterize in three ways, all of which are straight forward
One of them is to make three cauteries or four in a row according to the length of the spleen, following the figure of the cautery which we mentioned concerning the liver.
And be between every cauterization the quantity of breadth of a finger, or more or less.
And be the manner of cauterization as we said in the cauterization of the liver equally
And do not press the hand with the cauterization: and let the patient lie relaxed above his back.
And another manner of cauterization is: that you have two rings holding the cauterization, as we said in the chapter on the dislocation of the humerus: and elevate the skin which is over the spleen, where the patient's elbow bends: and elevate your elevation as much as the width of the patient's body, so that the cauteries fall according to the length of the patient's body.
Then insert two rings with the fire alight until when the cauterization has penetrated the skin from the other side: then remove the cauterization: four cauteries will remain
And if you wish to cauterize with another cauterization which has three rings.
Then take care of the cauterization after you have sent it away to emit pus for many days: for it is better to confer than to leave anything remaining from the cure
In the case of cauterization for hydrops.
The cauterization does not fall in hydrops, except as it is burned itself.
When you treat hydrops with the methods of treatment which we said in the section on wound care, and the cure does not appear, then it is necessary to cauterize it with four cauterizations around the navel, one on the stomach, one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two on the back between the vertebrae, and one in the centre of the chest, and one in the centre of the abdomen: and let the quantity of depth of the cauterization be close to the thickness of the skin
Then discharge the opened cautery, so that pus may issue forth over a long period of time.
Do not leave the patient unattended after the cautery has been used: for two intentions must be applied to him at the same time: and it will hasten his recovery with the help of God.
The shape of the cautery which is to be used for the belly is like a nail: as it has been previously described; and that which is to be used for the back is like an olive, as it has been previously described
As regards the cautery of the feet and legs...
When they swell in Hydropsicus, and are filled with yellow water: it is necessary to cauterize over the back of the foot between the heel and the ankle: and hold your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it: then raise your hand: and do not move it at all
The yellow water will rise up, and the cautery must be in this shape.
Then make on each leg two cauteries at the ankle, and make the cautery with the tip of the cautery: and make the cautery according to the length of the leg, one below the knee and the other above it at the middle of the leg: and make two cauteries over every hip: and discharge the opened cautery without treatment over a long period of time: so that some of the water may remain from it: then care for the limb as we have said before
As regards the cautery in the solution of the belly...

Method of cautery for haemorrhoids.
Chapter 6.
When there are many old haemorrhoids in the rectum, or one, and they are made by gross, cold or damp humours, and are not cured by what has been said, then burn three cauteries over the lower spine below the ribs in a triangular shape, and burn under the navel as if with two fingers
And if you think that his stomach is hardened, and that his food does not digest, and that he vomits fluid from his face, then burn him with a large cautery over the stomach according to what has been said: and burn over the spleen and the other over the tail of the pancreas, with the clamp open for a while: then care for him until he is healed.

On how to cauterize the Ancham in dislocation
When moisture of the mucous is exuded at the foot of the Ancham, and is the cause of its displacement from its place: and the sign of that is when one limb hangs longer than the other when compared with the limb at the same level: and the place of dislocation is found in that cavity
Therefore it is necessary to cauterize the diseased part above the foot of the Ancham with a cauterium of a circle: after which you must draw a sign around the circumference of the foot: and let the foot itself fall in the middle of the circle

On how to cauterize in Sciatica
When pain occurs in the bone of the ankle, and the cause of that is coldness and moisture: the physician must treat the patient with that which we have mentioned in the treatise, and not otherwise; for it will vanish. Then it is necessary to remove the patient from the humours by means of foul pills, or artificial pills, or the like. Then cauterize it.
And the mode of cauterization in this is by two methods: either with a cautery with burnings, or with fire.
Cauterization with fire is according to many methods.
One of them is that one should cauterize over the bone of the ankle itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make the depth good, or bad And there should be space between every two cauteries equal to the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be round
When, however, the cautery is made in the middle over the bone of the ankle itself. Then there are four cauteries.
And if you cauterize in a circle, whose shape precedes the form of the dislocation of the ankle, one: so that it should contain the whole ankle
And burn the thickness of the whole skin
This is the mode of cauterization in Sciatica, when the pain is adherent to the ankle itself, and does not extend up to the knee and leg
If, however, it extends up to the knee and leg, then cauterize with two cauteries over the knee, over the place where the patient feels pain there, and cauterize your fourth finger towards the heel: and let the cautery be triangular
The depth of the burn should be in accordance with the depth of the blistering of the skin.
If the patient complains that the pain extends up to the toes, then burn there where the burn of a point, or a triangle, or a square, or many, is sufficient for that area.</start_of_turn>
If he complains of pain under the knee, then burn there with a single lancet.</start_of_turn>
In all your burnings, take care that you do not reach the nerves or great artery, and that you do not cause any lasting damage to the patient's body.</start_of_turn>
I have seen one who was burned on the thigh by those who were burning above the knee, and they completed their burning, and the limb became swollen, until the foot was completely black, and all was perforated and corrupted. Then there followed solution of the belly and death.
If there is pain in two parts together, burn both of them in the same way.</start_of_turn>
And some wise men have said concerning the burning of an abscess that this is its manner.</start_of_turn Make a mark like that of iron, whose diameter is half the palm: and let it be at a distance from the orifice equal to the thickness of the thumb nail, or less. And within this there is to be a third part like itself.</start_of_turn
And there should be space between every mark equal to the quantity of the thumb joint: and let the marks be opened from two parts: and let their height be like a knot, or two knots. And make a handle of iron well adapted to the marks.</start_of_turn
Then it is ignited in fire until it turns red, and shoots sparks: then it is placed upon a cushion over the painful side resting on the sound side. So it is cauterized with three round cautery instruments in one vessel.
Then it is left for three days. Then it is plastered with butter: and the wound is opened for many days. Then care for it with unguent until it is healed
Albucasis says, with regard to this kind of cautery, of the sons of the physicians, we use it little, because of its fearsome appearance: and because of this, few expect it over it
But indeed from the good cautery instruments it has its effect on him who uses it, and finds its place with it
The cautery, however, with the physicians who are burned by it, is like two companions who have a perforated arm, in which the heart of its vein comes out from the air, or from iron, the length of the wall: of which two knots or as many as are in their height.
And let there be space between each of these quantities equal to the thickness of a finger, and let there be an opening below and above: and let them contain themselves inside, according to this form.
Then place it upon a cushion over the painful side resting on the sound side And compress your hand over the cushion much Then pour between two circles of lukewarm water, which is warmed with fire a little, and keep it for an hour: and the patient will endure the biting of it, and even its touch, for indeed he finds biting like fire until it rests.
Then elevate your hand with the instrument, and draw hot water from the whole basin with sweet water: then let it go for three days.
And put butter on it, until the black of the wound has subsided: then let it go for a few days, and pus will come out of it. This is the ultimate remedy.
Then care for it with unguents, until it heals.
If the pain extends up to the hip or the thigh: make for it a basin containing water, as you did in the basin before
This is the way of hot water: and I have written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicine. Take alkali, and burnt lime ground together in equal parts: there should be two of each: and put them into a new basin, the lower part of which is perforated with a small hole, according to the quantity of the radius: and put under the bottom of the basin another basin filled with water: and pour over the alkali and lime sweet water, which should cover both by a finger: and when you have pressed them with your hand with a good compression: let the basin go, until the acute water of the lower basin has descended.
Then gather up the whole water, and pour it over another lime: and cool, until it recovers
These are indeed strong and acute, which are administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of the rest of the limbs. Because it makes the operation of fire itself
And among the physicians, when they cauterize the basin, even as for testicles, and mastic, and nails, and lime with soap, it is so that both are mixed together.
Galen also reports that an ancient physician treated a wound of the anus and a sciatica: and praised his skill. He also says that no other treatment was needed, and that it was healed by means of a single bath.
He is accustomed to take from the beard of a young man: if one cannot find one of these, take fat, pure and mixed: and apply it to the anus, where the pain is, or to the thigh or hip: and bind it, and leave it for three hours, or for as long as the patient feels relief from the pain Then put him into a bath.
When his body is soft, put him into the bath. For the pain departs, and he is healed
And you know that no other caustic should be used with these medicines, except after the evacuation of the body.
Dioscorides also says that the dung of goats, when burned with vinegar, brings relief to a sciatica: and it burns in this way. Take wool, and soak it in old oil, and apply it to the deep place which is between the thumb of the foot and the heel, and is closer to the heel
Then take the dry goat dung and burn it.
Then put it on the wool and leave it until it is extinguished. Do this again. Do not cease doing this until the sense of pain has passed away from the anus, and rest has been taken from the pain
And this method of cautery is called the cautery of Vaccinum.
Of the cautery for the pain of the back
When there is pain in the back from many causes, or from a wound, or from a blow, or from excessive evacuation, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and moist matter: and the cautery is not useless, except for one kind alone, which is made from the infusion of cold matter.
It is necessary therefore after evacuation of the patient with foetid pills, and things like these, to make three lines across the back where there is pain, as wide as the breadth of the palm of the hand, and to burn with the cautery five cauteries in every line, or more according to the tolerance of the patient or the extent of his pain: and to make the cautery with the point of the cautery
And if you will, burn three or four cauteries with the middle cautery point, according to this form.
Of the way of cauterizing in the hernia of the abdomen
This disease often happens to young children.
And the sign of its inception in children is: when there is a stricture in the bellybutton with vomiting and elevation, and movement: and you will find it in the last vertebra of the back and the nodes of the back, which begin to bulge out over the rest of the vertebrae

Of the care of water which accumulates in the heads of children.
Chapter I.
Know that this ailment often happens to children at birth: or when the midwife tightens the head of the child without gentleness.
And sometimes also from an occult cause which is not known
And I have not seen this ailment in anyone except children: and concerning all those whom I have seen suffer from it, I have seen no benefit from surgery in it.
And I have seen among children whose head was full of water, and the head would swell up every day, until they could not sit on their own because of the size of their head: and the moisture increased until they died
And this moisture is either accumulated between the skin and the bone: or is accumulated under the bone over the cartilage
And the operation in this case, if the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the swelling is slight, then it is necessary to make a single incision in the middle of the head, of the length of two knots, until the moisture is cured
This is the shape of a sponge.
If there is too much moisture, and the sponge is large, then make two incisions, according to this shape
If the moisture is under the bone, and its sign is that the fluid spills out from every part of the head: and the water is drained when you press your hand into the inside, and it does not remain hidden: then it is necessary to make three incisions in the middle of the head, according to this manner.
And after the incision, extract all the moisture. Then string the incisions with silk and wool Then suture it up from above with wine and oil until the fifth day.
Then loosen the ligament, and care for the wound with tension and oiling.
And do not make the head tight with the stitches. And feed the patient with little dry food until the limb is comfortable and healed
And another way of making an incision is to consider the size of the abscess and the collection of water
For sometimes it is in the back more, or in the cheek, or in the right, or in the left.
Proceed therefore with the incision where you see the abscess and the collection of water: and cut it according to what you are able to do
And observe, that you do not cut an artery, and there is no excessive bleeding, and the patient dies from that bleeding along with the evacuation of the moisture

And concerning the care of the wound in the autumn.
Every wound in the autumn falls into four kinds: either a mineral stone, or one like stone, such as iron and lead: or it is of plant origin, such as chickpea and beans: or it is a fluid substance, such as water, vinegar and blood, and things like these: or something that comes from an animal
When a wound in the autumn falls upon a stone, or a kind of stone that does not come from the earth, and does not grow in the autumn, it exposes the autumn to the earth: if you wash away the stone, then distil from the oil of violets or sage something from the vinegar Then manage the extraction of it [the foreign body], and make it firm with pressure, and apply ointment to the nostrils beside the pressure, after you have placed around the circumference of the ear a plug of linen or wool, and extended the ear upwards.
Many things proceed with this care.

If they come out with the pressure, that is good.
And if not, then manage the extraction of it with a blunt needle of small diameter
If they do not come out by this, then make a hole in the ear with a wire, and introduce the end of the wire into the opening of the ear many times, and apply ointment that is around the wire with fat, so that there is no air except for the wire: then draw it out with your hand with strong traction

If it does not yield to extraction, then grasp a thin, flexible sponge according to this shape
And carry out the excision of that kind from the grains that fall into the ear, and do not make it so, when you think that one of them is already softened by the moisture of the ear, until you have put it against many hurdles: then remove it with hooks, or with fine tweezers, or with suction, as we have said, for its extraction alleviates it.
However, in water which enters the ear, it is necessary that the patient perform a sneeze with the head downwards: and immediately pour a little warm fat over the ear: and let it rest upon that ear which is in the water If thereby it comes out, it is good.
And if not: then grasp many stones, according to the length of a finger, tight, soft, and warm them with fire: and let the patient put one of his ears into the opening of the ear: and let him spit out one of his toes from that side, and strike with another stone upon the stone which is in the ear Do not cease doing this until all the water is expelled
And thus water goes out like this, so that you take from the charcoal or from the sponge one, and introduce its extremity one into the ear: and raise up the other extremity with fire, until most of it is consumed by fire. And do thus again with another sponge, and make this one much larger, until all the water has gone out: and draw out the same with a tube according as it is said in the stone
In the extraction of an animal that is within the ear, if it is small of body, as a flea, and such as it, take care of it as I said in the explanation.
But if it is of great body, which appears to sense: then manage the extraction of it with the hand and with hooks: and thus it is easier for all who hold it in the ear
And when worms are generated in the ear, when you have treated it as we said in the explanation, and in the treatise on distillations, and it does not yield: then it is necessary to burn the ear in the sun. If anything appears there from the worms, then draw it out with the hand, or with fine hooks.
If nothing appears there, then take a tube, which has a narrow lower part and a wide upper part: and introduce its lower extremity into the ear according to the capacity which the sick ear tolerates: then withdraw it with great suction. Do thus repeatedly until all the worms have gone out.
If they do not obey you in their exit, then smear around the circumference of the tube with grease, as I said in the stone
When they do not go out as we said: then manage distillations which the ancient ones are experts in for the extermination of worms: and you will find it in the treatise on distillations.
And let your effusion be such as that which flows out with oil and medicines into the ear with this instrument, whose shape is depicted here. Like wax, which is made from silver or gold, lower it tightly, in which there is a small hole, wide above
Let it be such that the driving force which is in the curvature of the tube is made of air centered And if you wish, take a ball of cotton, and place it at the end of the tube: then pour oil, or gum, or whatever you wish of these medicines into the tube: and let it be in the ear: then insert the ball of cotton onto the cotton and compress it moderately, until the oil is driven into the curvature of the ear, and the patient feels it inside: and that which is poured into the ear, let it be already warmed with a little fire: and beware that nothing is distilled in it which is cold and wet: for medicines do not tolerate that.

As for the care of an inflamed auricle.
When some infants emerge from the mother's womb unpierced.
And sometimes it happens to some people that their earwax is in the ear from a wound, or from being born with it.
And this earwax, when it is in the deep part of the ear canal, does not follow usual methods: and when it happens at the outer part of the ear canal, and follows the usual methods.
That which happens in the deep part of the ear, and which does not understand the aspect of it, is in many situations difficult to heal
And as for that which follows the usual methods, it is necessary to put the ear of the patient in the sun, and to press in it: then if you see the apparent earwax, open it with a fine spatula, whose form is this which follows, let its extremity be in which there is a slight width, whose part is acute: and the rest of the spatula should be soft on both sides: so that it does not hurt the ear
If there is a swelling from meat that has risen in the ear: then hold one finger under the ear, and press with ease until the whole flesh is removed.
If the swelling is deep in the ear: then take a slender needle, thread it, and burnish it with fire: then pass it into the ear meat
If you feel swelling with pain, which an infirm person has with difficulty hearing, try to open it with ease: and be careful, lest you damage the nerves of the ear.
Then put into the ear a wick according to the quantity of the hole you have opened in the eardrum: do this for a few days, until you are certain of the healing of the wound.
Or take a wick, soak it in rosewater, sprinkle it over charcoal that has been ground to powder, and use it like that.
If you have put the wick in the ear and it has become loose: then you must take out the wick, and put in another one, which you will put in a vessel containing rosewater, until the swelling has subsided: then care for it until it has healed
If blood flows: then immerse a sponge or bandage in cold water, and put it on the ear: and use the rest of the treatment which expels the blood stated in the treatise on distillation.

Chapter IX
Many things happen in the palpebrae of the eye that assimilate with Crandinis in its hardness and its roughness, and because of this it is called Grand: and it is the accumulation of thick moisture in the upper and lower palpebrae.
The operation is thus done in the eye, as you will consider, if there is a Grand proceeding from the palpebra, which appears from the palpebra and moves to all parts, and this is easy to do

About the care of the eyelids.
Chapter 10.
The secret is a kind of grease which is generated in the upper eyelid: and most of all it happens in children: and it weighs down the eyes of them, and causes them to be blind in the mornings, and they are not able to see the light of the sun, because the tears run down their faces always, and because of that the tears lie over their face always, and over their eyes they are always wet, and their eyelids are always soft because of the swelling: and the prominence of the secret is seen in the eye, and when you press with your fingers, you feel the secret between your fingers.
And the way to treat it is for the patient to put his head on your lap

Regarding the methods of treating the eye, that is, when the eyelid is softened, from which it results that the eye becomes red as it should not be.

Chapter XII
Regarding the elevation of hairs piercing the eye with the needle
The operation in this is that you take a fine needle and introduce it into the silk thread, which is soft Then you join the extremities of it and make knots at each end with a fine knot: and let the length of the thread be as much as a palm of the hand
Then you make another fine thread and pass it under this one in a short space, and knot the extremities of it if you wish.
Then you place the patient's head in your hand, and it should be near the cheek so that the operation is clear: because the operation is slight, or even almost negligible
Then insert the needle with the thread at the root of the eyelid, and make it penetrate the eyelid quickly, until you have pulled out the natural hair
Then draw out the hair until above the thread: and introduce into the thread the tip of the hair: if there is one, or two, or three, not more
Then draw your hand away with it, until the hair with the thread comes out of the eyelid with the natural hair.
If, however, the thread is drawn out and the hair does not come out with it: draw out the thread to the lower part, with the thread which you made in it, until the thread comes out of the upper hole, and you see the eye: then you draw out the thread and the needle, and close the eye: and leave the eye closed for two days, or three, until the hair has grown back in its place, and has become stronger than before
If the hair is short, either associate with it a long hair from natural hair, and elevate with it: or dismiss it, until it extends after space, and then elevate it.

When this happens to the eye, it is called the Leporina.
This phenomenon is either natural or accidental
Accidental, therefore, is from the consolidation of a wound, or a section, or a cauterization, and the like

Chapter 15.
Concerning the adhesion of the eyelid to the conjunctiva, or the cornea.

On the incision of the nail and the elevation of the carnis lachrymarum.
On the incision of the nail and the elevation of the carnis lachrymarum.
You know that the nail is according to two modes. Or it is fleshy: and it is similar to soft wax, delicate Or it is not nervous, similar to frozen white moisture: which when it touches iron, or when you grasp it with a hook, it is broken off and does not remain in it
And both of these kinds do not begin, except from the greater lacrimal gland, until it has proceeded slowly, until it covers the useful thing, and excludes light and the movement of the eye
And the manner of working in its incision is: as you place your sickly head in your lap Then open its eyes, and elevate the eyelid with your hand Then gather the nail with a hook of a few doubloons, and stretch it upwards. Then grasp the point with a needle, and introduce it into the hair of the horse, and blood, or fat: and let the thread be strong, and double the end of the needle thin, and fix it in the middle of the nail: and pierce the nail with the needle, and ligate the nail with the thread, and stretch the nail upwards: and remove the outer layer of the nail following the pupil, as if you were shaving it with the nail until the last of it
And then cut the remainder in the root of the lacrimal gland with fine scissors, or with small forceps: and release the natural carnis lachrymalis, so that it does not cause excessive flow of tears from its incision
When the nail extends with a single loop: or with a thread, as we have said. Then it is to be pared back with a blunt spatula, whose form is like this
Beware, lest you touch the sensitive membrane of the cornea with the spatula, and cause a rupture, and perforate the pupil.
Then, after the incision, pour some powdered salt or mix it from barley flour, and leave it in for until tomorrow. Then care for it as is necessary, until it is healed
If the nail is neither sensitive nor does it contain marrow within, and if it does not bleed, then it is to be treated with many medicines, and it will heal as I have mentioned before
If you wish to make an incision, then open the eye of the patient, and take out the sharp and fine spatula, of moderate sharpness, according to this form. And remove the nail from above with care and precision If you see that it is becoming pale and brittle, and that it is cracking, and that it has split in two, then wash it out of your eye with barley flour or with red ochre or with salt: and instill the eye with something until tomorrow.
Then repeat the operation until it is complete Except that there is a soft callus in the eye: then leave it in place, and care for the callus until it is healed
Then repeat the operation above with care until it is healed
The swelling of the tear gland, if it causes great pain in the eye, is to be suspended with a loop, and a portion of it is to be cut away: and do not make the incision at the end, lest you cause the tears to leak out
Then stay in the tear duct with a red sponge, or made from spongewort, until it heals.

On the collection of the fat from the eye
Chapter 18.
The fat is a red wax which covers the eye, and hinders its operation: and it weakens the eye with the length of the days.
Therefore you must first consider, if the eye in which the fat is, is strong, and is not in any other illness besides the fat: then collect the fat from it
And it is necessary to command the patient to keep his head in your lap
Then suspend those waxes with one or two hooks, according to your prudence: and let the hook be of fine wire, doubled, according to this form, or two hooks graduated in one body, according to this form.
Then collect with fine forceps those waxes with diligence, and wash away the blood an hour after an hour, until you have verified that those waxes have been removed from the eye, and have dissolved: and beware lest you wound the eye with the edges of the spatula
And let your operation be in the middle of the day before the sun, and be firm in your operation so that you do not injure anything except the waxes.
When you have finished [administering the medicine], then distill into the eye a little of the green or red unguent: so that its sharpness may eat away what remains from the wound.
When it is not possible to collect all of that in an hour, then smear the eye with this [ointment], which will soothe the pain of the eye: and leave it for a few days, until the pain has subsided. And keep it away from heat: then repeat the procedure above until the eye is healed.

On the reduction of the Arissa to the nose.
Chapter XIX.
Physicians call the Arissa Fistula which is treated with cautery, or with acute medicine which burns, as she has previously mentioned
If it does not heal, then there is no skill in it: except that you should find the abscess at its origin and evacuate all the moisture which is in it and pus, until the bone is clean
When the bone is thus cleansed, and the cavity is filled with corruption or blackness, then seal it up with an instrument of this shape
This is called the Asperation of the head
Make it from iron without a handle, and let its head be round like an egg, which is pierced with the point of a lime-stone, or with the point of an awl or with a fine point: and put it on the place of the corrupted bone.
Then rotate it between your fingers, and press your hand lightly, until you know that the corruption is gone: and do this several times.
Then restore the place with astringent substances.
If therefore the locus is solidified and a carbuncle arises in it, and the course of the disease is severed: and it remains for forty days, and does not recur, and does not abate, and does not happen in that place again: then you know that the patient is already healed.
If not, then it is not in that part, except to reduce the swelling to the size of a pinhole, according to this fashion.
And it is thus, that you perceive the second bone with iron, or with acute medicine: and when it is detected, then grasp firmly according to this fashion, whether the outer extremity be of iron, triangular: and its wood be extended as far as the extremity, like urine
Then place that upon the bone itself: and let it be near the tear-duct: and extend your hand from the eye a little. Then withdraw your hand with the instrument until it penetrates the bone, and feel that it is infirm: thereby that you will know that the wound has come out through that, when you keep your hand on your nose
Therefore then restore the place with astringent medicines that exude, as I have taught you.
When therefore a carbuncle arises in the flesh, and the place is solidified: then the matter which flowed outwards returns to the nose: thus indeed is it easier for it to be over the infirmity
On the reduction of the swelling of the eye.
Chapter 20
When the eye swells up completely, and does not yield to any document, neither by diminution: then it is necessary to dissolve the swelling: then perform a phlebotomy: afterwards apply warm compresses to the sky without making an incision, but with suction.
Then apply upon the eye a unguent made from acacia, aloe, oil, and ochre. Then bind over the eye a patch with many feathers
And as for the feathers, take fine wool, many of them, and fold every feather over four: make many of them: then put one over the other, as many as are needed for the eye: then bind over them with a strong cloth
Do it again with gentle pressure without cutting
Then remove the swelling, and keep the eye closed day and night.
If, however, the ligament is again softened, then it must be bound much more tightly: then remove the ligament after a day and a night, as we have said.
If thus you see the eye again redden, it is good: and if not, then bind over the eye again, the feathers, and the cloth, and the swelling, until it is healed.
About the incision of the edge of the eye
Chapter 21.
When it happens that the ligament is ruptured in the eye, then it comes out and proceeds outside the eyelids like a grain of sand, and is injured in the shape of a man because of this, and one must cut it: then the operation in this is as follows: and it is that you insert a needle into the root of the ligament from the lower part to the upper part
Then insert another needle into which is double thread from the lachrymal part, and make it penetrate: and remove the first needle according to its position.
Then cut the place of the double thread, and bind with it the part of the ligament around the needle: and bind it tightly.

And when you have tied the thread from every part with a circle of cloth, until you have added the eye a great prominence

On the care of the Alcomnatum.
Chapter XXII.
This ailment which is called Alcomnatum, is not anything other than health which is gathered in the eye, like water that descends and is not the ailment itself.
And the way to treat it is to make the patient sit on a prepared seat, or direct him to sit
Then take his head in your hands from two parts and move it until you feel health going down to the lower parts of your eyes Then fix it, and do not let it go down, and close your eyes: and the patient will see as well as before: and if it does not go down below, you know that it is water
If however the descent of health is not prepared with this which we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands. Then take a fine needle and find with it above the cornea the thickness of the conjunctiva with the tunica cornea in a circle, until the health comes out.
When the patient departs, then distill into the eye a warm water in which was mixed honey: or water in which you have cast barley groats and honey: then care for it with the remaining treatment until it is healed.
